The timestamp eventually used by Kafka depends on the timestamp type configured for\n * the topic.\n * <li>\n * If the topic is configured to use {@link org.apache.kafka.common.record.TimestampType#CREATE_TIME CreateTime},\n * the timestamp in the producer record will be used by the broker.\n * </li>\n * <li>\n * If the topic is configured to use {@link org.apache.kafka.common.record.TimestampType#LOG_APPEND_TIME LogAppendTime},\n * the timestamp in the producer record will be overwritten by the broker with the broker local time when it appends the\n * message to its log.\n * </li>\n * <p>\n * In either of the cases above, the timestamp that has actually been used will be returned to user in\n * {@link RecordMetadata}\n */\npublic class ProducerRecord<K, V> {\n\n    private final String topic;\n    private final Integer partition;\n    private final Headers headers;\n    private final K key;\n    private final V value;\n    private final Long timestamp;\n\n    /**\n     * Creates a record with a specified timestamp to be sent to a specified topic and partition\n     * \n     * @param topic The topic the record will be appended to\n     * @param partition The partition to which the record should be sent\n     * @param timestamp The timestamp of the record, in milliseconds since epoch. If null, the producer will assign\n     *                  the timestamp using System.currentTimeMillis().\n     * @param key The key that will be included in the record\n     * @param value The record contents\n     * @param headers the headers that will be included in the record\n     */\n    public ProducerRecord(String topic, Integer partition, Long timestamp, K key, V value, Iterable<Header> headers) {\n        if (topic == null)\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Topic cannot be null.\");\n        if (timestamp != null && timestamp < 0)\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\n                    String.format(\"Invalid timestamp: %d. Timestamp should always be non-negative or null.\", timestamp));\n        if (partition != null && partition < 0)\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\n                    String.format(\"Invalid partition: %d. Partition number should always be non-negative or null.\", partition));\n        this.topic = topic;\n        this.partition = partition;\n        this.key = key;\n        this.value = value;\n        this.timestamp = timestamp;\n        this.headers = new RecordHeaders(headers);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Creates a record with a specified timestamp to be sent to a specified topic and partition\n     *\n     * @param topic The topic the record will be appended to\n     * @param partition The partition to which the record should be sent\n     * @param timestamp The timestamp of the record, in milliseconds since epoch. If null, the producer will assign the\n     *                  timestamp using System.currentTimeMillis().\n     * @param key The key that will be included in the record\n     * @param value The record contents\n     */\n    public ProducerRecord(String topic, Integer partition, Long timestamp, K key, V value) {\n        this(topic, partition, timestamp, key, value, null);\n    }\n\n    /**\n 43→ *\n    44→ * <ul>\n    45→ *   <li>{@link OperatorIOMetricGroup#getNumRecordsInCounter()} (highly recommended)\n    46→ *   <li>{@link OperatorIOMetricGroup#getNumBytesInCounter()} (recommended)\n must make sure this method is non-blocking.\n    66→     *\n    67→     * <p>Although the implementation can emit multiple records into the given ReaderOutput, it is\n    68→     * recommended not doing so. Instead, emit one record into the ReaderOutput and return a {@link\n    69→     * InputStatus#MORE_AVAILABLE} to let the caller thread know there are more records available.\n    70→     *\n    71→     * @return The InputStatus of the SourceReader after the method invocation.\n    72→     */\n    73→    InputStatus pollNext(ReaderOutput<T> output) throws Exception;\n    74→\n    75→    /**\n    76→     * Checkpoint on the state of the source.\n    77→     *\n    78→     * @return the state of the source.\n    79→     */\n    80→    List<SplitT> snapshotState(long checkpointId);\n    81→\n    82→    /**\n    83→     * Returns a future that signals that data is available from the reader.\n    84→     *\n    85→     * <p>Once the future completes, the runtime will keep calling the {@link\n    86→     * #pollNext(ReaderOutput)} method until that method returns a status other than {@link\n    87→     * InputStatus#MORE_AVAILABLE}. After that, the runtime will again call this method to obtain\n    88→     * the next future. Once that completes, it will again call {@link #pollNext(ReaderOutput)} and\n    89→     * so on.\n    90→     *\n    91→     * <p>The contract is the following: If the reader has data available, then all futures\n    92→     * previously returned by this method must eventually complete. Otherwise the source might stall\n    93→     * indefinitely.\n    94→     *\n    95→     * <p>It is not a problem to have occasional \"false positives\", meaning to complete a future\n    96→     * even if no data is available. However, one should not use an \"always complete\" future in\n    97→     * cases no data is available, because that will result in busy waiting loops calling {@code\n    98→     * pollNext(...)} even though no data is available.\n    99→     *\n   100→     * @return a future that will be completed once there is a record available to poll.\n   101→     */\n   102→    CompletableFuture<Void> isAvailable();\n   103→\n   104→    /**\n   105→     * Adds a list of splits for this reader to read. This method is simply providing connectors with more expressive APIs the\n   148→     * opportunity to update all subscriptions at once.\n   149→     *\n   150→     * <p>This is currently used to align the watermarks of splits, if watermark alignment is used\n   151→     * and the source reads from more than one split.\n   152→     *\n   153→     * <p>The default implementation throws an {@link UnsupportedOperationException} where the\n   154→     * default implementation will be removed in future releases. After that, the runtime will again call this method to obtain\n     * the next future. Once that completes, it will again call {@link #pollNext(ReaderOutput)} and\n     * so on.\n     *\n     * <p>The contract is the following: If the reader has data available, then all futures\n     * previously returned by this method must eventually complete. Otherwise the source might stall\n     * indefinitely.\n     *\n     * <p>It is not a problem to have occasional \"false positives\", meaning to complete a future\n     * even if no data is available. However, one should not use an \"always complete\" future in\n     * cases no data is available, because that will result in busy waiting loops calling {@code\n     * pollNext(...)} even though no data is available.\n     *\n     * @return a future that will be completed once there is a record available to poll.\n     */\n    CompletableFuture<Void> isAvailable();\n\n    /**\n     * Adds a list of splits for this reader to read. This method is called when the enumerator\n     * assigns a split via {@link SplitEnumeratorContext#assignSplit(SourceSplit, int)} or {@link\n     * SplitEnumeratorContext#assignSplits(SplitsAssignment)}.\n     *\n     * @param splits The splits assigned by the split enumerator.\n     */\n    void addSplits(List<SplitT> splits);\n\n    /**\n     * This method is called when the reader is notified that it will not receive any further\n     * splits.\n     *\n     * <p>It is triggered when the enumerator calls {@link\n     * SplitEnumeratorContext#signalNoMoreSplits(int)} with the reader's parallel subtask.\n     */\n    void notifyNoMoreSplits();\n\n    /**\n     * Handle a custom source event sent by the {@link SplitEnumerator}. This method is called when\n     * the enumerator sends an event via {@link SplitEnumeratorContext#sendEventToSourceReader(int,\n     * SourceEvent)}.\n     *\n     * <p>This method has a default implementation that does nothing, because most sources do not\n     * require any custom events.\n     *\n     * @param sourceEvent the event sent by the {@link SplitEnumerator}.\n     */\n    default void handleSourceEvents(SourceEvent sourceEvent) {}\n\n    /**\n     * We have an empty default implementation here because most source readers do not have to\n     * implement the method.\n     *\n     * @see CheckpointListener#notifyCheckpointComplete(long)\n     */\n    @Override\n    default void notifyCheckpointComplete(long checkpointId) throws Exception {}\n\n    /**\n     * Pauses or resumes reading of individual source splits.\n     *\n     * <p>Note that no other methods can be called in parallel, so updating subscriptions can be\n     * done atomically. This method is simply providing connectors with more expressive APIs the\n     * opportunity to update all subscriptions at once.\n     *\n     * <p>This is currently used to align the watermarks of splits, if watermark alignment is used\n     * and the source reads from more than one split.\n     *\n     * <p>The default implementation throws an {@link UnsupportedOperationException} where the\n     * default implementation will be removed in future releases. To be compatible with future\n     * releases, it is recommended to implement this method and override the default implementation.\n     *\n     * @param splitsToPause the splits to pause\n     * @param splitsToResume the splits to resume\n     */\n    @PublicEvolving\n    default void pauseOrResumeSplits(\n            Collection<String> splitsToPause, Collection<String> splitsToResume) {\n        throw new UnsupportedOperationException(\n                \"This source reader does not support pausing or resuming splits which can lead to unaligned splits.\\n\"\n                        + \"Unaligned splits are splits where the output watermarks of the splits have diverged more than the allowed limit.\\n\"\n                        + \"It is highly discouraged to use unaligned source splits, as this leads to unpredictable\\n\"\n                        + \"watermark alignment if there is more than a single split per reader. It is recommended to implement pausing splits\\n\"\n                        + \"for this source. At your own risk, you can allow unaligned source splits by setting the\\n\"\n                        + \"configuration parameter `pipeline.watermark-alignment.allow-unaligned-source-splits' to true.\\n\"\n                        + \"Beware that this configuration parameter will be dropped in a future Flink release.\");\n    }\n}\n","numLines":173,"startLine":1,"totalLines":173}}}

In either case, this method should be reentrant, meaning that\n    43→     * the next fetch call should just resume from where the last fetch call was waken up or\n    44→     * interrupted. The implementation could either read from a single split\n * or from multiple splits.\n *\n * @param <E> the element type.\n * @param <SplitT> the split type.\n */\n@PublicEvolving\npublic interface SplitReader<E, SplitT extends SourceSplit> extends AutoCloseable {\n\n    /**\n     * Fetch elements into the blocking queue for the given splits. The fetch call could be blocking\n     * but it should get unblocked when {@link #wakeUp()} is invoked. In that case, the\n     * implementation may either decide to return without throwing an exception, or it can just\n     * throw an interrupted exception. In either case, this method should be reentrant, meaning that\n     * the next fetch call should just resume from where the last fetch call was waken up or\n     * interrupted. It is up to the implementer to either read all the records of the split or to\n     * stop reading them at some point (for example when a given threshold is exceeded). In that\n     * later case, when fetch is called again, the reading should restart at the record where it\n     * left off based on the {@code SplitState}.\n     *\n     * @return the Ids of the finished splits.\n     * @throws IOException when encountered IO errors, such as deserialization failures.\n     */\n    RecordsWithSplitIds<E> fetch() throws IOException;\n\n    /**\n     * Handle the split changes. This call should be non-blocking.\n     *\n     * <p>For the consistency of internal state in SourceReaderBase, if an invalid split is added to\n     * the reader (for example splits without any records), it should be put back into {@link\n     * RecordsWithSplitIds} as finished splits so that SourceReaderBase could be able to clean up\n     * resources created for it.\n     *\n     * <p>For the consistency of internal state in SourceReaderBase, if a split is removed, it\n     * should be put back into {@link RecordsWithSplitIds} as finished splits so that\n     * SourceReaderBase could be able to clean up resources created for it.\n     *\n     * @param splitsChanges the split changes that the SplitReader needs to handle.\n     */\n    void handleSplitsChanges(SplitsChange<SplitT> splitsChanges);\n\n    /** Wake up the split reader in case the fetcher thread is blocking in {@link #fetch()}. */\n    void wakeUp();\n\n    /**\n     * Pauses or resumes reading of individual splits readers.\n     *\n     * <p>Note that no other methods can be called in parallel, so it's fine to non-atomically\n     * update subscriptions. This method is simply providing connectors with more expressive APIs\n     * the opportunity to update all subscriptions at once.\n     *\n     * <p>This is currently used to align the watermarks of splits, if watermark alignment is used\n     * and the source reads from more than one split.\n     *\n     * <p>The default implementation throws an {@link UnsupportedOperationException} where the\n     * default implementation will be removed in future releases. To be compatible with future\n     * releases, it is recommended to implement this method and override the default implementation.\n     *\n     * @param splitsToPause the splits to pause\n     * @param splitsToResume the splits to resume\n     */\n    default void pauseOrResumeSplits(\n            Collection<SplitT> splitsToPause, Collection<SplitT> splitsToResume) {\n        throw new UnsupportedOperationException(\n                \"This split reader does not support pausing or resuming splits which can lead to unaligned splits.\\n\"\n                        + \"Unaligned splits are splits where the output watermarks of the splits have diverged more than the allowed limit.\\n\"\n                        + \"It is highly discouraged to use unaligned source splits, as this leads to unpredictable\\n\"\n                        + \"watermark alignment if there is more than a single split per reader. It is recommended to implement pausing splits\\n\"\n                        + \"for this source. At your own risk, you can allow unaligned source splits by setting the\\n\"\n                        + \"configuration parameter `pipeline.watermark-alignment.allow-unaligned-source-splits' to true.\\n\"\n                        + \"Beware that this configuration parameter will be dropped in a future Flink release.\");\n    }\n}\n","numLines":102,"startLine":1,"totalLines":102}}}

       }\n   539→    }\n   540→\n   541→    /**\n   542→     * A wrapper around {@link SourceOutput} that counts the number of records during the current\n   543→     * rate-limiting window.\n   544→         recordsOfCurrentWindow++;\n   587→        }\n   588→\n   589→        @Override\n   590→        public void collect(T record, long timestamp) {\n   591→            sourceOutput.collect(record, 604→        /** Resets the recordsOfCurrentWindow to 0. */\n   605→        public void resetWindowRecordCount() {\n   606→            recordsOfCurrentWindow = 0;\n   607→        }\n   608→    }\n java.util.concurrent.CompletableFuture;\nimport java.util.function.Function;\n\nimport static org.apache.flink.util.Preconditions.checkState;\n\n/**\n * An abstract implementation of {@link This class allows user to just\n * provide a {@link SplitReader} and snapshot the split state.\n *\n * <p>This implementation provides the following metrics out of the box:\n *\n * <ul>\n *   <li>{@link OperatorIOMetricGroup#getNumRecordsInCounter()}\n * </ul>\n *\n * @param <E> The rich element type that contains information for split state update or timestamp\n *     extraction.\n * SourceReaderBase<E, T, SplitT extends SourceSplit, SplitStateT>\n        implements SourceReader<T, SplitT> {\n    private static final Logger LOG = LoggerFactory.getLogger(SourceReaderBase.class);\n\n    /** A queue to buffer the elements fetched by the fetcher thread. */\n    private final FutureCompletingBlockingQueue<RecordsWithSplitIds<E>> elementsQueue;\n\n    /** The state of the splits. */\n    private final Map<String, SplitContext<T, SplitStateT>> splitStates;\n\n    /** The record emitter to handle the records read by the protected final Configuration config;\n\n    private final Counter numRecordsInCounter;\n\n    /** The context of this source reader. */\n    protected SourceReaderContext context;\n\n    /** The latest fetched batch of records-by-split from the split reader. */\n    @Nullable private RecordsWithSplitIds<E> currentFetch;\n\n    @Nullable private SplitContext<T, SplitStateT> currentSplitContext;\n    @Nullable private SourceOutput<T> currentSplitOutput;\n\n    /** Indicating whether the SourceReader will be assigned more splits or not. */\n    private boolean noMoreSplitsAssignment;\n\n    @Nullable protected final RecordEvaluator<T> eofRecordEvaluator;\n\n    /** Indicating whether the SourceReader supports rate limiting or not. */\n    private final acquiring permission from {@link #rateLimiter}. */\n    @Nullable private CompletableFuture<Void> rateLimitPermissionFuture;\n\n    /**\n     * The primary constructor for the source reader.\n     *\n     * <p>The reader will use a handover queue sized as configured via {@link\n     * SourceReaderOptions#ELEMENT_QUEUE_CAPACITY}.\n     */\n    public SourceReaderBase(\n            SplitFetcherManager<E, SplitT> splitFetcherManager,\n            RecordEmitter<E, T, SplitStateT> recordEmitter,\n            Configuration config,\n            SourceReaderContext context) {\n        this(splitFetcherManager, recordEmitter, null, config, context, null);\n    }\n\n    public SourceReaderBase(\n            SplitFetcherManager<E, SplitT> splitFetcherManager,\n this(splitFetcherManager, recordEmitter, eofRecordEvaluator, config, context, null);\n    }\n\n    public SourceReaderBase(\n            SplitFetcherManager<E, SplitT> splitFetcherManager,\n            RecordEmitter<E, T, SplitStateT> recordEmitter,\n            @Nullable RecordEvaluator<T> eofRecordEvaluator,\n            Configuration config,\n            SourceReaderContext context,\n            @Nullable RateLimiterStrategy<SplitT> rateLimiterStrategy) {\n        this.elementsQueue = splitFetcherManager.getQueue();\n        this.splitFetcherManager = splitFetcherManager;\n        this.recordEmitter = recordEmitter;\n        this.splitStates = new HashMap<>();\n        this.options = new SourceReaderOptions(config);\n        this.config = config;\n        this.context = context;\n        this.noMoreSplitsAssignment = false;\n        this.eofRecordEvaluator = eofRecordEvaluator;\n        this.rateLimitingEnabled = rateLimiterStrategy != null;\n        numRecordsInCounter = context.metricGroup().getIOMetricGroup().getNumRecordsInCounter();\n\n        rateLimiter =\n                rateLimitingEnabled\n                        ? rateLimiterStrategy.createRateLimiter(context.currentParallelism())\n                        : null;\n        LOG.info(\n                \"Rate limiting of SourceReader is {}\",\n                rateLimitingEnabled ? \"enabled\" : \"disabled\");\n        rateLimitPermissionFuture = CompletableFuture.completedFuture(null);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void start() {}\n\n    @Override\n    public InputStatus pollNext(ReaderOutput<T> output) throws Exception {\n        // make sure we have a fetch we are working on, or move to the next\n        RecordsWithSplitIds<E> recordsWithSplitId = this.currentFetch;\n        if (recordsWithSplitId == null) {\n            recordsWithSplitId = getNextFetch(output);\n            if (recordsWithSplitId == null) {\n                return trace(finishedOrAvailableLater());\n            }\n        }\n        if (rateLimitingEnabled) {\n            return pollNextWithRateLimiting(recordsWithSplitId, output);\n        } else {\n            return pollNextWithoutRateLimiting(recordsWithSplitId, output);\n        }\n    }\n\n    private InputStatus pollNextWithoutRateLimiting(\n            RecordsWithSplitIds<E> recordsWithSplitId, ReaderOutput<T> output) throws Exception {\n        // we need to loop here, in case we may have to go across splits\n        while (true) {\n            // Process one record.\n            final E record = recordsWithSplitId.nextRecordFromSplit();\n            if (record != null) {\n                // emit the record.\n                numRecordsInCounter.inc(1);\n                recordEmitter.emitRecord(record, currentSplitOutput, currentSplitContext.state);\n                LOG.trace(\"Emitted record: {}\", record);\n                // We always emit MORE_AVAILABLE here, even though we do not strictly know whether\n                // more is available. If nothing more is available, the next invocation will find\n                // this out and return the correct status.\n                // That means we emit the occasional 'false positive' for availability, but this\n                // saves us doing checks for every record. Ultimately, this is cheaper.\n                return trace(InputStatus.MORE_AVAILABLE);\n            } else if (!moveToNextSplit(recordsWithSplitId, output)) {\n                // The fetch is done and we just discovered that and have not emitted anything, yet.\n                // We need to move to the next fetch. As a shortcut, we call pollNext() here again,\n                // rather than emitting nothing and waiting for the caller to call us again.\n                return pollNext(output);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    private InputStatus pollNextWithRateLimiting(\n            RecordsWithSplitIds<E> recordsWithSplitId, ReaderOutput<T> output) throws Exception {\n        // make sure we have a fetch we are working on, or move to the next\n        while (true) {\n            // Check if the previous record count reached the limit of rateLimiter.\n            if (!rateLimitPermissionFuture.isDone()) {\n                return trace(InputStatus.MORE_AVAILABLE);\n            }\n            // Process one record.\n            final E record = recordsWithSplitId.nextRecordFromSplit();\n            if (record != null) {\n                // emit the record.\n                numRecordsInCounter.inc(1);\n                recordEmitter.emitRecord(record, currentSplitOutput, currentSplitContext.state);\n                LOG.trace(\"Emitted record: {}\", record);\n                RateLimitingSourceOutputWrapper<T> rateLimitingSourceOutputWrapper =\n                        (RateLimitingSourceOutputWrapper<T>) currentSplitOutput;\n                if (rateLimitingSourceOutputWrapper.getRecordsOfCurrentWindow() > 0) {\n                    // Acquire permit from rateLimiter.\n                    rateLimitPermissionFuture =\n                            rateLimiter\n                                    .acquire(\n                                            rateLimitingSourceOutputWrapper\n                                                    .getRecordsOfCurrentWindow())\n                                    .toCompletableFuture();\n                }\n                rateLimitingSourceOutputWrapper.resetWindowRecordCount();\n\n                // We always emit MORE_AVAILABLE here, even though we do not strictly know whether\n                // more is available. If nothing more is available, the next invocation will find\n                // this out and return the correct status.\n                // That means we emit the occasional 'false positive' for availability, but this\n                // saves us doing checks for every record. Ultimately, this is cheaper.\n                return trace(InputStatus.MORE_AVAILABLE);\n            } else if (!moveToNextSplit(recordsWithSplitId, output)) {\n                // The fetch is done and we just discovered that and have not emitted anything, yet.\n                // We need to move to the next fetch. As a shortcut, we call pollNext() here again,\n                // rather than emitting nothing and waiting for the caller to call us again.\n                return pollNext(output);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    private InputStatus trace(InputStatus status) {\n        LOG.trace(\"Source reader status: {}\", status);\n        return status;\n    }\n\n    @Nullable\n    private RecordsWithSplitIds<E> getNextFetch(final ReaderOutput<T> output) {\n        splitFetcherManager.checkErrors();\n\n        LOG.trace(\"Getting next source data batch from queue\");\n        final RecordsWithSplitIds<E> recordsWithSplitId = elementsQueue.poll();\n        if (recordsWithSplitId == null || !moveToNextSplit(recordsWithSplitId, output)) {\n            // No element available, set to available later if needed.\n            return null;\n        }\n\n        currentFetch = recordsWithSplitId;\n        return recordsWithSplitId;\n    }\n\n    private void finishCurrentFetch(\n            final RecordsWithSplitIds<E> fetch, final ReaderOutput<T> output) {\n        currentFetch = null;\n        currentSplitContext = null;\n        currentSplitOutput = null;\n\n        final Set<String> finishedSplits = fetch.finishedSplits();\n        if (!finishedSplits.isEmpty()) {\n            LOG.info(\"Finished reading split(s) {}\", finishedSplits);\n            Map<String, SplitStateT> stateOfFinishedSplits = new HashMap<>();\n            for (String finishedSplitId : finishedSplits) {\n                stateOfFinishedSplits.put(\n                        finishedSplitId, splitStates.remove(finishedSplitId).state);\n                output.releaseOutputForSplit(finishedSplitId);\n            }\n            onSplitFinished(stateOfFinishedSplits);\n        }\n\n        fetch.recycle();\n    }\n\n    private boolean moveToNextSplit(\n            RecordsWithSplitIds<E> recordsWithSplitIds, ReaderOutput<T> output) {\n        final String nextSplitId = recordsWithSplitIds.nextSplit();\n        if (nextSplitId == null) {\n            LOG.trace(\"Current fetch is finished.\");\n            finishCurrentFetch(recordsWithSplitIds, output);\n            return false;\n        }\n\n        currentSplitContext = splitStates.get(nextSplitId);\n        checkState(currentSplitContext != null, \"Have records for a split that was not registered\");\n\n        Function<T, Boolean> eofRecordHandler = null;\n        if (eofRecordEvaluator != null) {\n            eofRecordHandler =\n                    record -> {\n                        if (!eofRecordEvaluator.isEndOfStream(record)) {\n                            return false;\n                        }\n                        SplitT split =\n                                toSplitType(currentSplitContext.splitId, currentSplitContext.state);\n                        splitFetcherManager.removeSplits(Collections.singletonList(split));\n                        return true;\n                    };\n        }\n        if (rateLimitingEnabled) {\n            rateLimiter.notifyAddingSplit(\n                    this.toSplitType(\n                            this.currentSplitContext.splitId, this.currentSplitContext.state));\n        }\n        currentSplitOutput =\n                currentSplitContext.getOrCreateSplitOutput(\n                        output, eofRecordHandler, rateLimitingEnabled);\n        LOG.trace(\"Emitting records from fetch for split {}\", nextSplitId);\n        return true;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public CompletableFuture<Void> isAvailable() {\n        return currentFetch != null\n                ? FutureCompletingBlockingQueue.AVAILABLE\n                : elementsQueue.getAvailabilityFuture();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public List<SplitT> snapshotState(long checkpointId) {\n        List<SplitT> splits = new ArrayList<>();\n        splitStates.forEach((id, context) -> splits.add(toSplitType(id, context.state)));\n        return splits;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void notifyCheckpointComplete(long checkpointId) throws Exception {\n        splitStates.forEach(\n                (id, context) -> {\n                    if (rateLimitingEnabled) {\n                        rateLimiter.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId);\n                    }\n                });\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void addSplits(List<SplitT> splits) {\n        LOG.info(\"Adding split(s) to reader: {}\", splits);\n        // Initialize the state for each split.\n        splits.forEach(\n                s ->\n                        splitStates.put(\n                                s.splitId(), new SplitContext<>(s.splitId(), initializedState(s))));\n        // Hand over the splits to the split fetcher to start fetch.\n        splitFetcherManager.addSplits(splits);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void notifyNoMoreSplits() {\n        LOG.info(\"Reader received NoMoreSplits event.\");\n        noMoreSplitsAssignment = true;\n        elementsQueue.notifyAvailable();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void handleSourceEvents(SourceEvent sourceEvent) {\n        LOG.info(\"Received unhandled source event: {}\", sourceEvent);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void pauseOrResumeSplits(\n            Collection<String> splitsToPause, Collection<String> splitsToResume) {\n        splitFetcherManager.pauseOrResumeSplits(splitsToPause, splitsToResume);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void close() throws Exception {\n        LOG.info(\"Closing Source Reader.\");\n        splitFetcherManager.close(options.sourceReaderCloseTimeout);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Gets the number of splits the reads has currently assigned.\n     *\n     * <p>These are the splits that have been added via {@link #addSplits(List)} and have not yet\n     * been finished by returning them from the {@link SplitReader#fetch()} as part of {@link\n     * RecordsWithSplitIds#finishedSplits()}.\n     */\n    public int getNumberOfCurrentlyAssignedSplits() {\n        return splitStates.size();\n    }\n\n    // -------------------- Abstract method to allow different implementations ------------------\n\n    /** Handles the finished splits to clean the state if needed. */\n    protected abstract void onSplitFinished(Map<String, SplitStateT> finishedSplitIds);\n\n    /**\n     * When new splits are added to the reader. The initialize the state of the new splits.\n     *\n     * @param split a newly added split.\n     */\n    protected abstract SplitStateT initializedState(SplitT split);\n\n    /**\n     * Convert a mutable SplitStateT to immutable SplitT.\n     *\n     * @param splitState splitState.\n     * @return an immutable Split state.\n     */\n    protected abstract SplitT toSplitType(String splitId, SplitStateT splitState);\n\n    // ------------------ private helper methods ---------------------\n\n    private InputStatus finishedOrAvailableLater() {\n        final boolean allFetchersHaveShutdown = splitFetcherManager.maybeShutdownFinishedFetchers();\n        if (!(noMoreSplitsAssignment && allFetchersHaveShutdown)) {\n            return InputStatus.NOTHING_AVAILABLE;\n        }\n        if (elementsQueue.isEmpty()) {\n            // We may reach here because of exceptional split fetcher, check it.\n            splitFetcherManager.checkErrors();\n            return InputStatus.END_OF_INPUT;\n        } else {\n            // We can reach this case if we just processed all data from the queue and finished a\n            // split,\n            // and concurrently the fetcher finished another split, whose data is then in the queue.\n            return InputStatus.MORE_AVAILABLE;\n        }\n    }\n\n    // ------------------ private helper classes sourceOutput;\n\n        private SplitContext(String splitId, SplitStateT state) {\n            this.state = state;\n            this.splitId = splitId;\n        }\n\n        SourceOutput<T> records after receiving the eof record. */\n    private static final class SourceOutputWrapper<T> implements SourceOutput<T> {\n        final SourceOutput<T> sourceOutput;\n        final Function<T, sourceOutput.collect(record);\n            }\n        }\n\n        @Override\n        public void collect(T record, long timestamp) {\n            if (!isEndOfStreamReached(record)) {\n                sourceOutput.collect(record, timestamp);\n            }\n        }\n\n        /**\n         * Judge and handle the eof record.\n         *\n         * @return whether the record is the eof record.\n    recordsOfCurrentWindow = 0;\n        }\n    }\n}\n","numLines":610,"startLine":1,"totalLines":610}}}

`notifyCheckpointComplete()` calls `sourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)` which propagates to the Kafka connector for offset commit; `handleOperatorEvent()` routes `AddSplitEvent` → `sourceReader.addSplits()`\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### 1. Kafka Producer Path\n```\nUser data (K, V)\n  → ProducerRecord<K,V>  [topic, partition, key, value, timestamp, headers]\n  → Serializer<K>.serialize()  →  byte[] serializedKey\n  → Serializer<V>.serialize()  →  byte[] serializedValue\n  → KafkaProducer.doSend()\n      → RecordAccumulator.append()  [batches by partition]\n  → Sender (background I/O thread)\n      → NetworkClient.send()  →  ProduceRequest  →  Kafka Broker\n```\n\n### 2. Kafka Consumer Path\n```\nKafka Broker\n  → FetchResponse (raw RecordBatch bytes per TopicPartition)\n  → FetchBuffer (ring buffer in consumer)\n  → FetchCollector.fetchRecords()\n      → Deserializer<K>.deserialize()  →  typed key K\n      → Deserializer<V>.deserialize()  →  typed value V\n  → ConsumerRecord<K,V>  [topic, partition, offset, timestamp, leaderEpoch, key, value]\n  → ConsumerRecords<K,V>  returned by KafkaConsumer.poll()\n  → OffsetAndMetadata  [offset+1, optional leaderEpoch]\n      → KafkaConsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)\n```\n\n### 3. Flink Source API\n```\nSource<T, SplitT, EnumChkT>  [factory, runs at compile/planning time]\n  → SplitEnumerator<SplitT, EnumChkT>  [JobManager: discovers & assigns splits]\n      → snapshotState(checkpointId) → EnumChkT  [serialized by getEnumeratorCheckpointSerializer()]\n  → SourceReader<T, SplitT>          [TaskManager: reads assigned splits]\n      → pollNext(ReaderOutput<T>)    [non-blocking; called from task main thread]\n      → snapshotState(checkpointId)  → List<SplitT>\n      → notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)\n      → addSplits(List<SplitT>)\n```\n\n### 4. Flink Connector-Base Framework\n```\nSourceReaderBase<E, T, SplitT, SplitStateT>   implements SourceReader<T, SplitT>\n  ├── SplitFetcherManager<E, SplitT>\n  │     └── SplitFetcher threads (one or more)\n  │           └── SplitReader<E, SplitT>.fetch()  [blocking, background thread]\n  │                 → RecordsWithSplitIds<E>  [pushed to FutureCompletingBlockingQueue]\n  ├── FutureCompletingBlockingQueue<RecordsWithSplitIds<E>>  [thread-safe handover]\n  └── RecordEmitter<E, T, SplitStateT>.emitRecord(E, SourceOutput<T>, SplitStateT)\n        → SourceOutput<T>.collect(T)  [emits to Flink pipeline]\n```\n\n### 5. Flink Serde Boundary\n```\nOn source (reading from Kafka):\n  Kafka Deserializer<byte[]>   [built into Kafka consumer internals, produces raw bytes]\n  → DeserializationSchema<T>.deserialize(byte[])   [Flink layer, produces typed T]\n  → RecordEmitter.emitRecord()  → SourceOutput<T>\n\nOn sink (writing to Kafka):\n  Flink data T\n  → SerializationSchema<T>.serialize(T)   [Flink layer, produces byte[]]\n  → Kafka Serializer<byte[]>  (passthrough ByteArraySerializer)\n  → KafkaProducer.send(ProducerRecord<byte[], byte[]>)\n```\n\n### 6. Flink Runtime: SourceOperator Checkpoint → Kafka Offset Commit\n```\nCheckpointBarrier injected by Flink runtime\n  → SourceOperator.snapshotState(StateSnapshotContext ctx)\n      → sourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId)      [SourceReaderBase]\n          → splitStates.forEach → toSplitType(id, state)\n          → returns List<SplitT>  [each split carries current offset position]\n      → readerState.update(List<SplitT>)               [stored in ListState<byte[]>]\n\nCheckpoint completes (all barriers aligned at downstream operators)\n  → SourceOperator.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)\n      → sourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)   [SourceReaderBase]\n          → [Kafka connector override] KafkaSourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete()\n              → KafkaSourceFetcherManager or SplitReader\n                  → KafkaConsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)\n                     [commits offsets stored in split state at checkpoint time]\n```\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### How Kafka's Consumer API Is Wrapped by Flink's SplitReader\n\nIn the Flink Kafka connector (external repo, `apache/flink-connector-kafka`), a `KafkaSplitReader` implements Flink's `SplitReader<ConsumerRecord<byte[], byte[]>, KafkaPartitionSplit>`. The `fetch()` method wraps `KafkaConsumer.poll(Duration)`, translating Kafka's `ConsumerRecords` into Flink's `RecordsWithSplitIds`. The split concept maps directly to Kafka topic-partitions: each `KafkaPartitionSplit` encodes a `TopicPartition` plus a starting offset and optional stopping offset.\n\nThe `SplitFetcherManager` manages one or more `SplitFetcher` threads running `KafkaSplitReader`. Because `KafkaConsumer` is not thread-safe, each fetcher thread owns its own consumer instance. The manager uses `FutureCompletingBlockingQueue` to safely hand fetched batches from the I/O thread to Flink's main task thread, where `SourceReaderBase.pollNext()` drains them.\n\n### The Dual Serialization Boundary\n\nThere are **two distinct serialization layers**:\n\n1. **Kafka's Serializer/Deserializer** (Kafka-internal): On the producer side, `KafkaProducer.doSend()` calls `Serializer<K>.serialize()` and `Serializer<V>.serialize()` to convert typed objects into `byte[]` before appending to the `RecordAccumulator`. On the consumer side, `FetchCollector` uses `Deserializer<K>` and `Deserializer<V>` inside `fetchRecords()` to convert raw `RecordBatch` bytes into typed `ConsumerRecord<K,V>`.\n\n2. **Flink's DeserializationSchema / SerializationSchema** (Flink-level): Flink's `DeserializationSchema<T>` operates on the `byte[]` value from the `ConsumerRecord` (i.e., after Kafka's own `Deserializer` has already run). In practice, when the Flink Kafka connector is configured with `ByteArrayDeserializer` on the Kafka side, the raw bytes flow through unchanged to `DeserializationSchema.deserialize(byte[])`, which converts them into the Flink pipeline's output type `T`. Similarly, `SerializationSchema<T>.serialize(T)` produces `byte[]` that is then passed to `KafkaProducer` using a `ByteArraySerializer`.\n\nThe result is that both layers exist in a pipeline:\n```\nWire bytes → Kafka Deserializer → byte[] → Flink DeserializationSchema → Flink type T\n```\nMost deployments collapse Kafka's layer to a no-op `ByteArrayDeserializer` and put all conversion logic in the Flink schema.\n\n### How Checkpoint Completion Triggers Kafka Offset Commits\n\nFlink's exactly-once guarantee for Kafka consumption is implemented via a two-phase handshake:\n\n**Phase 1 — Snapshot** (`snapshotState`): When a Flink checkpoint barrier arrives at the `SourceOperator`, `snapshotState(ctx)` calls `sourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId)`. `SourceReaderBase` collects the current `SplitStateT` (which, for Kafka, includes the next-to-consume offset per `TopicPartition`) and serializes it into Flink's `ListState`. No Kafka `commitSync` occurs yet.\n\n**Phase 2 — Completion** (`notifyCheckpointComplete`): Once all operators in the pipeline have successfully completed the checkpoint (barriers have aligned and state has been persisted), the JobManager notifies each task. `SourceOperator.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)` calls `sourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)`. In the Kafka connector's `KafkaSourceReader`, this triggers `KafkaConsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)` with the offsets that were captured during the snapshot phase, durably persisting consumer group progress to Kafka's `__consumer_offsets` topic.\n\nThis two-phase design ensures that Kafka offsets are only committed after the corresponding Flink state is safely checkpointed. If a failure occurs between snapshot and completion, Flink restores from checkpoint, re-reads from the snapshotted offsets, and the consumer group offset commit is simply not done — guaranteeing at-least-once (or exactly-once when combined with transactional sinks).\n\n### Consumer Group Coordination Model\n\nKafka's native consumer group protocol (coordinated via a `GroupCoordinator` broker) is typically **bypassed** when Flink uses the FLIP-27 `KafkaSource`. Instead of subscribing via `subscribe(Collection<String>)` and relying on Kafka's rebalance protocol, the connector uses `KafkaConsumer.assign(Collection<TopicPartition>)` in each `KafkaSplitReader`. The Flink `KafkaSplitEnumerator` (on the JobManager) is responsible for discovering topic partitions (via Kafka admin APIs) and assigning them to `SourceReader` instances. This means Flink's own fault-tolerance mechanism (checkpoint + split reassignment on failure) replaces Kafka's rebalance-based recovery, giving Flink full control over exactly-once semantics.\n\n### Thread Architecture\n\n**Kafka producer**:\n- User thread: calls `KafkaProducer.send()` → serializes → appends to `RecordAccumulator` (thread-safe)\n- `Sender` I/O thread (background `Runnable`): drains accumulator, sends `ProduceRequest` via `NetworkClient`\n\n**Kafka consumer** (within Flink):\n- `SplitFetcher` thread(s): each owns a `KafkaConsumer`, calls `poll()` (blocking), publishes `RecordsWithSplitIds` to `FutureCompletingBlockingQueue`\n- Flink task main thread (mailbox): calls `SourceReaderBase.pollNext()`, drains queue, calls `RecordEmitter.emitRecord()` to push records downstream\n\nThis architecture decouples Kafka's blocking I/O from Flink's event-loop, while preserving the single-threaded constraint of `KafkaConsumer`.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nStreaming data flows from a Kafka broker into Flink through a layered pipeline: `KafkaConsumer.poll()` (running in a dedicated `SplitFetcher` thread) fetches raw `RecordBatch` bytes, which Kafka's internal `FetchCollector`/`Deserializer` converts into `ConsumerRecord<byte[], byte[]>`; these are then handed off via `FutureCompletingBlockingQueue` to Flink's task main thread, where `SourceReaderBase` drives a `RecordEmitter` that applies Flink's `DeserializationSchema` to produce the final typed records emitted into the streaming DAG. Checkpointing is coordinated via a two-phase commit: `SourceOperator.snapshotState()` stores current Kafka offsets inside Flink's `ListState`, and only after the checkpoint is confirmed complete does `notifyCheckpointComplete()` trigger `KafkaConsumer.commitSync()` — ensuring Kafka consumer group offsets are durably committed only after Flink's recovery point is safely persisted.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":126,"cache_read_input_tokens":72462,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":126,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":18,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"f76b5ac8-b3be-4b20-a0b3-a15f6bb80c71","uuid":"ab30cd64-25da-4676-8fbb-b65de8ae9b68"}

`notifyCheckpointComplete()` calls `sourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)` which propagates to the Kafka connector for offset commit; `handleOperatorEvent()` routes `AddSplitEvent` → `sourceReader.addSplits()`\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### 1. Kafka Producer Path\n```\nUser data (K, V)\n  → ProducerRecord<K,V>  [topic, partition, key, value, timestamp, headers]\n  → Serializer<K>.serialize()  →  byte[] serializedKey\n  → Serializer<V>.serialize()  →  byte[] serializedValue\n  → KafkaProducer.doSend()\n      → RecordAccumulator.append()  [batches by partition]\n  → Sender (background I/O thread)\n      → NetworkClient.send()  →  ProduceRequest  →  Kafka Broker\n```\n\n### 2. Kafka Consumer Path\n```\nKafka Broker\n  → FetchResponse (raw RecordBatch bytes per TopicPartition)\n  → FetchBuffer (ring buffer in consumer)\n  → FetchCollector.fetchRecords()\n      → Deserializer<K>.deserialize()  →  typed key K\n      → Deserializer<V>.deserialize()  →  typed value V\n  → ConsumerRecord<K,V>  [topic, partition, offset, timestamp, leaderEpoch, key, value]\n  → ConsumerRecords<K,V>  returned by KafkaConsumer.poll()\n  → OffsetAndMetadata  [offset+1, optional leaderEpoch]\n      → KafkaConsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)\n```\n\n### 3. Flink Source API\n```\nSource<T, SplitT, EnumChkT>  [factory, runs at compile/planning time]\n  → SplitEnumerator<SplitT, EnumChkT>  [JobManager: discovers & assigns splits]\n      → snapshotState(checkpointId) → EnumChkT  [serialized by getEnumeratorCheckpointSerializer()]\n  → SourceReader<T, SplitT>          [TaskManager: reads assigned splits]\n      → pollNext(ReaderOutput<T>)    [non-blocking; called from task main thread]\n      → snapshotState(checkpointId)  → List<SplitT>\n      → notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)\n      → addSplits(List<SplitT>)\n```\n\n### 4. Flink Connector-Base Framework\n```\nSourceReaderBase<E, T, SplitT, SplitStateT>   implements SourceReader<T, SplitT>\n  ├── SplitFetcherManager<E, SplitT>\n  │     └── SplitFetcher threads (one or more)\n  │           └── SplitReader<E, SplitT>.fetch()  [blocking, background thread]\n  │                 → RecordsWithSplitIds<E>  [pushed to FutureCompletingBlockingQueue]\n  ├── FutureCompletingBlockingQueue<RecordsWithSplitIds<E>>  [thread-safe handover]\n  └── RecordEmitter<E, T, SplitStateT>.emitRecord(E, SourceOutput<T>, SplitStateT)\n        → SourceOutput<T>.collect(T)  [emits to Flink pipeline]\n```\n\n### 5. Flink Serde Boundary\n```\nOn source (reading from Kafka):\n  Kafka Deserializer<byte[]>   [built into Kafka consumer internals, produces raw bytes]\n  → DeserializationSchema<T>.deserialize(byte[])   [Flink layer, produces typed T]\n  → RecordEmitter.emitRecord()  → SourceOutput<T>\n\nOn sink (writing to Kafka):\n  Flink data T\n  → SerializationSchema<T>.serialize(T)   [Flink layer, produces byte[]]\n  → Kafka Serializer<byte[]>  (passthrough ByteArraySerializer)\n  → KafkaProducer.send(ProducerRecord<byte[], byte[]>)\n```\n\n### 6. Flink Runtime: SourceOperator Checkpoint → Kafka Offset Commit\n```\nCheckpointBarrier injected by Flink runtime\n  → SourceOperator.snapshotState(StateSnapshotContext ctx)\n      → sourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId)      [SourceReaderBase]\n          → splitStates.forEach → toSplitType(id, state)\n          → returns List<SplitT>  [each split carries current offset position]\n      → readerState.update(List<SplitT>)               [stored in ListState<byte[]>]\n\nCheckpoint completes (all barriers aligned at downstream operators)\n  → SourceOperator.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)\n      → sourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)   [SourceReaderBase]\n          → [Kafka connector override] KafkaSourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete()\n              → KafkaSourceFetcherManager or SplitReader\n                  → KafkaConsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)\n                     [commits offsets stored in split state at checkpoint time]\n```\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### How Kafka's Consumer API Is Wrapped by Flink's SplitReader\n\nIn the Flink Kafka connector (external repo, `apache/flink-connector-kafka`), a `KafkaSplitReader` implements Flink's `SplitReader<ConsumerRecord<byte[], byte[]>, KafkaPartitionSplit>`. The `fetch()` method wraps `KafkaConsumer.poll(Duration)`, translating Kafka's `ConsumerRecords` into Flink's `RecordsWithSplitIds`. The split concept maps directly to Kafka topic-partitions: each `KafkaPartitionSplit` encodes a `TopicPartition` plus a starting offset and optional stopping offset.\n\nThe `SplitFetcherManager` manages one or more `SplitFetcher` threads running `KafkaSplitReader`. Because `KafkaConsumer` is not thread-safe, each fetcher thread owns its own consumer instance. The manager uses `FutureCompletingBlockingQueue` to safely hand fetched batches from the I/O thread to Flink's main task thread, where `SourceReaderBase.pollNext()` drains them.\n\n### The Dual Serialization Boundary\n\nThere are **two distinct serialization layers**:\n\n1. **Kafka's Serializer/Deserializer** (Kafka-internal): On the producer side, `KafkaProducer.doSend()` calls `Serializer<K>.serialize()` and `Serializer<V>.serialize()` to convert typed objects into `byte[]` before appending to the `RecordAccumulator`. On the consumer side, `FetchCollector` uses `Deserializer<K>` and `Deserializer<V>` inside `fetchRecords()` to convert raw `RecordBatch` bytes into typed `ConsumerRecord<K,V>`.\n\n2. **Flink's DeserializationSchema / SerializationSchema** (Flink-level): Flink's `DeserializationSchema<T>` operates on the `byte[]` value from the `ConsumerRecord` (i.e., after Kafka's own `Deserializer` has already run). In practice, when the Flink Kafka connector is configured with `ByteArrayDeserializer` on the Kafka side, the raw bytes flow through unchanged to `DeserializationSchema.deserialize(byte[])`, which converts them into the Flink pipeline's output type `T`. Similarly, `SerializationSchema<T>.serialize(T)` produces `byte[]` that is then passed to `KafkaProducer` using a `ByteArraySerializer`.\n\nThe result is that both layers exist in a pipeline:\n```\nWire bytes → Kafka Deserializer → byte[] → Flink DeserializationSchema → Flink type T\n```\nMost deployments collapse Kafka's layer to a no-op `ByteArrayDeserializer` and put all conversion logic in the Flink schema.\n\n### How Checkpoint Completion Triggers Kafka Offset Commits\n\nFlink's exactly-once guarantee for Kafka consumption is implemented via a two-phase handshake:\n\n**Phase 1 — Snapshot** (`snapshotState`): When a Flink checkpoint barrier arrives at the `SourceOperator`, `snapshotState(ctx)` calls `sourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId)`. `SourceReaderBase` collects the current `SplitStateT` (which, for Kafka, includes the next-to-consume offset per `TopicPartition`) and serializes it into Flink's `ListState`. No Kafka `commitSync` occurs yet.\n\n**Phase 2 — Completion** (`notifyCheckpointComplete`): Once all operators in the pipeline have successfully completed the checkpoint (barriers have aligned and state has been persisted), the JobManager notifies each task. `SourceOperator.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)` calls `sourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)`. In the Kafka connector's `KafkaSourceReader`, this triggers `KafkaConsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)` with the offsets that were captured during the snapshot phase, durably persisting consumer group progress to Kafka's `__consumer_offsets` topic.\n\nThis two-phase design ensures that Kafka offsets are only committed after the corresponding Flink state is safely checkpointed. If a failure occurs between snapshot and completion, Flink restores from checkpoint, re-reads from the snapshotted offsets, and the consumer group offset commit is simply not done — guaranteeing at-least-once (or exactly-once when combined with transactional sinks).\n\n### Consumer Group Coordination Model\n\nKafka's native consumer group protocol (coordinated via a `GroupCoordinator` broker) is typically **bypassed** when Flink uses the FLIP-27 `KafkaSource`. Instead of subscribing via `subscribe(Collection<String>)` and relying on Kafka's rebalance protocol, the connector uses `KafkaConsumer.assign(Collection<TopicPartition>)` in each `KafkaSplitReader`. The Flink `KafkaSplitEnumerator` (on the JobManager) is responsible for discovering topic partitions (via Kafka admin APIs) and assigning them to `SourceReader` instances. This means Flink's own fault-tolerance mechanism (checkpoint + split reassignment on failure) replaces Kafka's rebalance-based recovery, giving Flink full control over exactly-once semantics.\n\n### Thread Architecture\n\n**Kafka producer**:\n- User thread: calls `KafkaProducer.send()` → serializes → appends to `RecordAccumulator` (thread-safe)\n- `Sender` I/O thread (background `Runnable`): drains accumulator, sends `ProduceRequest` via `NetworkClient`\n\n**Kafka consumer** (within Flink):\n- `SplitFetcher` thread(s): each owns a `KafkaConsumer`, calls `poll()` (blocking), publishes `RecordsWithSplitIds` to `FutureCompletingBlockingQueue`\n- Flink task main thread (mailbox): calls `SourceReaderBase.pollNext()`, drains queue, calls `RecordEmitter.emitRecord()` to push records downstream\n\nThis architecture decouples Kafka's blocking I/O from Flink's event-loop, while preserving the single-threaded constraint of `KafkaConsumer`.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nStreaming data flows from a Kafka broker into Flink through a layered pipeline: `KafkaConsumer.poll()` (running in a dedicated `SplitFetcher` thread) fetches raw `RecordBatch` bytes, which Kafka's internal `FetchCollector`/`Deserializer` converts into `ConsumerRecord<byte[], byte[]>`; these are then handed off via `FutureCompletingBlockingQueue` to Flink's task main thread, where `SourceReaderBase` drives a `RecordEmitter` that applies Flink's `DeserializationSchema` to produce the final typed records emitted into the streaming DAG. Checkpointing is coordinated via a two-phase commit: `SourceOperator.snapshotState()` stores current Kafka offsets inside Flink's `ListState`, and only after the checkpoint is confirmed complete does `notifyCheckpointComplete()` trigger `KafkaConsumer.commitSync()` — ensuring Kafka consumer group offsets are durably committed only after Flink's recovery point is safely persisted.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
